<Rating>5</Rating><Text>Kennels are clean and staff clearly care for the poor souls who end up here. They are always professional if a little too clinical but given what they see and how the public treats them it's to be expected. I think people leaving negative reviews aren't being realistic. We don't have the resources other municipalities have, low kill shelters are ideal but not always feasible. I hate that animals have to be euthanized or housed in cold kennels but that's the reality of it until people wake up and stop buying puppies from backyard breeders and puppy shops. We need mandatory spay neuter laws before we can reasonably expect low kill shelters in our community. In the interim I feel the resources allocated to Devore shelter are used well and the staff do the best they can.

I'm adopting another fur baby today, my 3rd from this shelter and I wish I could take more home! Bottom line before you say negative things about this specific shelter and it's policies, please consider your own choices and actions first. Do you sterilize all your pets and encourage neighbors friends and family to do so? Are you politically active, and do you vote? Do you know how your tax dollars are allocated and how your local city and state reps vote on animal rights issues? If your answer is you don't even know your state Rep then go back to the drawing board.</Text>< Pics>

< Text>
We went to Devore about three or four months ago looking for a dog. We found one we wanted but we were told that she had to be adopted through a rescue and shipped out in a hard crate because she had growled at someone. The dog was a husky and the main thing we noticed about her was how sweet she was so this was hard to believe. We were told if we could get a rescue to take her we could adopt her through the rescue. The staff said there was plenty of time to get this done because the shelter wasn‚Äôt full so there were no dogs on the kill list. The staff also gave us the name of their Facebook page and the name of a rescue they claimed to work close with. So we started looking into how to get the process done to get the dog and while we were at it we checked out Devore‚Äôs Facebook page. The Facebook page had a list of dogs on the kill list and nearly every dog we looked at in the shelter was on it including the dog we wanted. Many of the dogs were also listed as needing taken out in a hard crate. During our research we found out that the shelter made more money if the dogs were adopted through the rescues. Because these people blatantly lied to our faces about the kill list and the fact that many of the dogs listed for hard crates were very sweet I personally believe this organization is a crock. This situation affects my rating for this shelter but so does the health of the dogs that we saw there. Most of the dogs looked like they were starving or sick. Many of the dogs I could see their ribs. I sincerely hope that their quality of care for their animals has gone up since we have been there but I doubt it has.</Text>

<gmap_id>0x80c34e328a2987fb:0xdbec06e1341499db</gmap_id><Time>1518124336585</Time>< Text>
This place has been here in our community forever. When a dog ends up here it's because it was found running loose or it's owner has decided to relinquish it for "whatever" reason. This shelter doesn't have a choice the way some shelters do. They HAVE to take every stray or owner release on their catchment area.
The people who work here have, over the years, been exposed to some of the most awful, animal hating people you can imagine. They have had to euthanize thousands of the most beautiful adoptable dogs and cats simply because "their time was up" and new ones were brought in that day HAD to be taken in.
The facilities are old and we all agree the county is understaffed. They do the best they can with the resources they have.  Is the beautiful? NO. Do they do right by the animals? I believe they do. I have found them to be caring people that have had to "toughen up" their personalities in order to be able to do this most difficult work. In closing I'd like to say if you really like to save a life, rescue from the Devote shelter, at least start your search there.</Text>

< Text>
I am writing this review in great hope that it will shift the consciousness of anyone that is considering dumping their animal at an animal shelter that euthanizes animals. I know that you are probably thinking that someone will adopt your pet, or that some fantastic rescue group will step in and save your dog just in the nick of time. How I wish it were true that every single animal that sits in a kill shelter would be saved from taking their final breath waiting for a forever home that never materialized.

If you truly love your animal and can‚Äôt keep them for whatever reason, I ask that you do everything in your power to find them a loving forever home. As a volunteer at an animal shelter I can tell you that the most beautiful, loving, trustworthy, friendly animals in our communities are losing their lives there, don‚Äôt fool yourself into believing that they only euthanize feeble old animals, everyone is fair game, and everyone needs to be moved along to make room for the new batch of animals that are constantly coming through the shelter doors.

The shelters will tell you what can we do? We have no choice but to euthanize, this is a problem created by society, we‚Äôre cleaning up their mess by destroying these animals. Shelters will continue doing business this way. It‚Äôs up to us as citizens to step up to the plate and take care of our animals until they are old, there isn‚Äôt a day that goes by that they don‚Äôt give us every ounce of love that is inside of them, they run to the door to happily greet us when we get home from work, they cheer us up on our saddest days, and they are happy to share every minute of their lives with us. Don‚Äôt turn your back on your animal and betray them by dumping them at an animal shelter that kills animals.< /Text>

<Time>1362110987977< /Time><review>A few days ago, my children and I were on our way home in Rialto. We came across a dirty, white poodle casually walking in the street, oblivious to the cars around it. Being an animal lover, I had do do something. We pulled over, called out to the dog and he immediately ran over to us and jumped in the car. This dog had no collar on. On the drive home, I knew my husband was not going to be happy since we already had 4 dogs, two cats, 5 birds and a rabbit in our home. As much as we are a family of animal lovers, we simply did not have room in our home for another dog.

After a bit of research, I learned that I needed to take the dog to the Devore Animal Shelter, as this particular shelter services my neighborhood. I read the online reviews and the picture  created in my mind was that of a "dog concentration camp." Without much time and without any other options, I decided to take the dog there and see what the facility was like. If it was in fact, a horrible place, I was going to keep the dog, take care of him and try to locate his owner. If that was not possible, I was going to find a good home for him myself.

When we arrived at the facility, my daughter and I went in and explained the story behind the dog. I mentioned that my daughter was upset at having to leave him there. (she had also read the online reviews). The manager, Doug, offered to give us a tour of the facility, which he did. He took us all around the entire property and explained step by step what happens to the animals on the premises and how they are cared for. We saw the cat rooms, the aggressive dog area, the small dog area, the large dog area and the outside pens for the large farm animals. Doug explained in detail the engineering behind the kennels and how all areas are temperature controlled so the animals remained comfortable, regardless of the weather.

We toured the entire facility and saw approximately 50 cats and probably 75-100 dogs. The inside facility and outside grounds were very clean. I was quite impressed. After walking through the entire facility, I didn't see nor did I smell one dog turd. It certainly didn't smell like a rose garden, but it was a very clean and well-kept facility. All the animals I saw appeared to be well fed and well cared for. Doug was kind enough to spend about 45 minutes with us, explaining all the various aspects of the facility.

Many of the other posts talk about the "kill rate" of the shelter. While this certainly is a very unpleasant thought, it is a fact of life. Every day, healthy animals are euthanized because there are simply not enough homes for them. If every pet owner were responsible and made sure their animal was not allowed to reproduce indiscriminately, if every pet owner made sure their pets were properly chipped and tagged, if people did not dump unwanted pets out into the street for others to deal with, then there would be no need for animal shelters. The fact is, overpopulation exists and must be dealt with in the best way possible. After touring the facility, I felt quite comfortable leaving the stray dog there. While we were there, he was immediately photographed to be put on the website and had his health evaluated by a technician. I pray for this dog and hope he is either found by his owner or adopted by a loving family. If anyone is interested, he is a  white, male, poodle type dog with light brown patches on his back. Approximately 6-7 years old. He was very sweet, quiet and lovable. He was in my house for 4 days. He did not mess in the floor once and he got along quite well with my other 4 dogs. He was left at the shelter on 2/28/13.

After my first hand experience at this shelter, I would advise anyone looking for a pet to consider visiting a shelter first. There were so many beautiful animals waiting to be adopted. Big dogs. little dogs, poodles, and puppies. There was something for everyone. I had a very positive experience at the Devore Animal Shelter and I recommend it highly.<//review>< response>

< text>
The Food
I discovered this interesting place when ramen was the decision for lunch. They have this concept of broffee, which is ramen broth in a coffee cup. We ordered their Gyukotsu and Miso ramen along with their Pasture Raised Pork Bone Broth. Because this is Yuzu Ramen, we had to order the Yuzu Creme Brulee to finish off. The Gyukotsu came with ground beef, red onions, green beans, renkon (lotus root), and soft boiled egg. The miso had chashu, kikurage, green onions, sliced lemon, soft boiled egg, and chili pepper. Both ramen had the more traditional style noodle, and both were not bad. Though the taste of the broth is on the lighter side so it might be lacking in flavor for some. For me, I do enjoy the lighter broth. Though I do wish they give more meat for the Gyukotsu, it was a bit lacking. The Pasture Raised Pork Bone Broth or broffee was good, an interesting side addition to the meal. Last but not least, the Yuzu Creme Brulee was delicious, with a nice yuzu taste to it.

The Miscellaneous
Yuzu Ramen is a decent sized restaurant, for a ramen that is. The restaurant is in an L shape configuration, which is interesting. They have normal seating as well as bar style seating. I was trying to make a reservation but there weren't any available, so I was expecting long lines. But it wasn't super crowded and seating is first come first serve after ordering. The service was good, and the employees were sincere. The restaurant advertises their ingredients as organic with no additives or preservatives. They have a variety of categories on their menu, each with a few selections. There's also special timed items like their donburi for lunch and sushi for dinner. The prices are higher than the typical ramen places around the bay. But their menu is interesting, so I'll probably return to try some of the other selections.< /text>

< Review>
The Food
I discovered this interesting place when ramen was the decision for lunch. They have this concept of broffee, which is ramen broth in a coffee cup. We ordered their Gyukotsu and Miso ramen along with their Pasture Raised Pork Bone Broth. Because this is Yuzu Ramen, we had to order the Yuzu Creme Brulee to finish off. The Gyukotsu came with ground beef, red onions, green beans, renkon (lotus root), and soft boiled egg. The miso had chashu, kikurage, green onions, sliced lemon, soft boiled egg, and chili pepper. Both ramen had the more traditional style noodle, and both were not bad. Though the taste of the broth is on the lighter side so it might be lacking in flavor for some. For me, I do enjoy the lighter broth. Though I do wish they give more meat for the Gyukotsu, it was a bit lacking. The Pasture Raised Pork Bone Broth or broffee was good, an interesting side addition to the meal. Last but not least, the Yuzu Creme Brulee was delicious, with a nice yuzu taste to it.

The Miscellaneous
Yuzu Ramen is a decent sized restaurant, for a ramen that is. The restaurant is in an L shape configuration, which is interesting. They have normal seating as well as bar style seating. I was trying to make a reservation but there weren't any available, so I was expecting long lines. But it wasn't super crowded and seating is first come first serve after ordering. The service was good, and the employees were sincere. The restaurant advertises their ingredients as organic with no additives or preservatives. They have a variety of categories on their menu, each with a few selections. There's also special timed items like their donburi for lunch and sushi for dinner. The prices are higher than the typical ramen places around the bay. But their menu is interesting, so I'll probably return to try some of the other selections.<//Review>

<Pictures>None< /Pictures><Resp>None< /Resp>< review>
I've been to this place a number of times. Don't get me wrong, the ramen is very good (hearty, high quality and contains a number of ingredients), but the past few times I've been there I've noticed a decline in quality (broth seems watered down, portions smaller, etc). Unfortunately, if I'm paying 15 dollars for a bowl of ramen, I can't accept anything buy high quality.

The menu and servers have changed multiple times in two years, which suggests ownership has changed as well. Maybe this is the reason the food has declined. I don't know. All I can say is this place was a great place for us to go for a while, but I feel like it is on  a downward trend. Prove me wrong Yuzu!< /review>

<Text>Used to be my favorite. I live half a block away and when this place popped up, my family and I were thrilled. The first 3 or 4 times we went , we got GREAT service, Amazing food and saw the owner (dressed as waitstaff) often. Very humble guy with a eye for good service.

Last night 9/7/17, the Family and I walked in for the 1 year anniversary around 7:45pm. As we walked in, we were greeted as usual. Sat down at our table and ordered the same thing we always get. My Wife and Daughter got the Spicy Miso. I got the Gyukotsu or beef bone broth with no mustard or egg, mushrooms on the side and gluten free noodles.  I like most mushroom but they are like wine and I don't like them all.

Since I was removing a protein (egg)  and asked if I could possibly get more asparagus, the waitress (who I later found out was the floor manager) said she would ask the kitchen, AND NEVER CAME BACK. Honestly I did not think twice about it. I have never been disappointed with this place so I dismissed it as all is well and moved on.

Excited as I always am with this place, I was truly disappointed when my meal arrived. It came first with 7 sliced of mushroom, 1/2 of a stalk of asparagus and what I found out seconds later chewy tasteless meat. We just kind of stared at the bowl. I asked is half a stack of asparagus (a whole stalk that someone actually took the time to slice in half length wise) was the new normal and I was told by waitstaff "it is just a garnish". It is the ONLY vegetable in the entire dish. And as a point of reference this was never the case before. As most cooks know, asparagus has to be broken at this natural point or you get this hard ,chewy and stringy portion which is unpleasant. That was not done so 1/3 of my half asparagus was a loss.

After the check was paid for, which took 15 - 20 minutes to get and then get back, I asked to speak with the manager. The young lady came and I explained the situation she was like "Oh I'm sorry to hear that, let me go talk with the kitchen manager" and walked off. We sat there for about 5-10 minutes and was just out done. We left and made the decision to never come back.

I come from the food industry and have even had the experience of having my life taken over by a restaurant as the General Manager. Tasting food and working with small business is what I do daily now but inconsistent quality of food or service has me in damage control with my clients. I honestly may be more sensitive to it but i just want good food all the time since the price is the same all the time.

In the end, the broth was the same Amazing experience but with no vegetables, lowered quality of meat, and a inattentive waitstaff , I can drive a little further and get the food I expect from Noodle Theory or The Ramen Shop.<//Text>< Pics>

Update November 2019:
Service has gone way downhill which is really saying something considering service in the Bay Area is generally pretty poor. But yeah, no need to be standoffish. Also, vegetarian offering is really poor. "No substitutions" seems to be the new mantra.  Also, it's now $16 for a bowl of ramen. If the rent is too high, move somewhere else. But if you need to have those prices for a bowl of noodles, at least demand more of your wait staff. And, don't run out of anything that you carry on tap.

Instead of "give 'em a try", I'm changing the review to "avoid if possible". There are many better options in the area.

< Text>
My first few visits here had been wonderful. My most recent visit may just be my last.

On Sept. 14th, my partner and I decided to stop in for our third dinner here. I ordered a tonkatsu udon and my partner the spicy miso ramen.

Here's a quick summary of everything I found to be wrong during our experience: my meal arrived five minutes after my partner's, had the wrong noodle, it took a while before I could flag anyone's attention, I was asked if I wanted it remade, when I replied yes I was told it would be around 10 minutes before they could get to my order (which came across like my order would be put last in line), my partner's broth had too much miso paste, and there was no correction on the bill for the waitress's mistake. The restaurant staff made no effort to check in whatsoever to see how our meal was.

Our experiences prior to this visit have been nothing short of great, but I think their growing popularity may have affected the quality of this establishment.</Text>

< Text>
Underwhelming and expensive.

I had the vegetarian ramen. The broth was quite thick and lacked all of the umami-richness of their bone broths,  ending up more like a butternut squash soup than a ramen broth. The vegetable assortment in the ramen ranged from delightful (thin layers of squash and toasted lotus root) to unpleasant (fresh cherry tomatoes and a whole roasted okra too tough to bite through).

All in all, Shiba Ramen is only a few blocks away, less expensive and providing a better vegetarian experience.</Text>

<Resp>None< /Resp>< review>
I ate at Yuzu Ramen & Broffee for lunch a week after its opening.  I ordered the tonkotsu ramen.  Overall, I am mixed about the ramen:

Pros:
- rich broth
- fresh noodles
- delicious chashu (braised pork belly)
- perfectly cooked egg

Cons:
- broth flavors were muted.  it was almost too rich, such that you couldn't pick out any particular flavors.  you could tell there was a lot going on, but nothing in particular stood out.  in the end, i'm not sure if that's a good thing or a bad thing.  i did like it enough to finish the whole thing, something i don't normally do with other ramen broths given their saltiness.
- small portion
- expensive ($14)... wouldn't be too bad if the portion was bigger.

The service was fast (even though I was told it would take 45 minutes, it only took about 10) and friendly.

There is both indoor and outdoor seating.  The outdoor seating area is great on a sunny day.

I think the place has a lot of potential, but it is expensive for what you get.  If you're looking for super flavorful (i.e., spicy and salty) ramen, this might not be it.  However, the ramen here is satisfying, so much so that I drank up all of the broth.  I guess that is their "broffee".</review>

< review>
This is a really great ramen place.  The broth choices are all good. There's three of them. They have signs up in the restaurant talking about the health benefits of bone broth. I can't speak to that but I might do some research on it. I had the beef broth with thinly sliced beef, asparagus and ramen noodles. The other broths come with different noodles one of them is wide and wavy. The ramen noodles I had were the traditional long wavy skinny noodles. I also tried the mini poke don and it was excellent. Everything comes with these wonderfully soft boiled eggs cut in half. The egg on the Pokemon was cold and it warmed up in the broth when it came served with the ramen. The service was slow and unimpressive. But that's kind of to be expected for a brand new place I think. They made up for it in enthusiasm and quality. I would definitely go back. I want to try the other things on their menu. They have a nice selection of beer and sake. I can't speak to the wine because I didn't have any wine. One really cool thing about this place is that you can get everything ala carte. Meaning that you can have just the broth or you can add whatever you want to the broth. The menu is really really flexible especially for folks who may have different dietary restraints or requirements or desires.</review>
